padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">t</span></span></span></span></span> (table).</li>
<li>Wait for the dwarves to install the furniture</li>
<li>Using the <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_z.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui z.png" src="/images/1/13/Ui_z.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="35" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">z</span></span></span></span></span> (zones) menu, mark the room as an office, and then assign the office to your expedition leader (who should be both your bookkeeper and manager).</li>
<li>Hit <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_n.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui n.png" src="/images/7/7b/Ui_n.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="36" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">n</span></span></span></span></span> to verify that these positions now have the office they need (if so, the icon next to the position should no longer be red).</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Furniture">Furniture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Furniture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 45%;">
<div style="background: #0a0; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Different Names, Same Thing</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>As you've noticed, some things have different names based on what they're made of (for example, chairs vs. thrones and chests vs. coffers) even if they're functionally the same (material almost never makes a difference). <a href="/index.php/Furniture#Furniture_types_with_multiple_names" title="Furniture">Here's a list.</a>
</p><p><a href="/index.php/Bed" title="Bed">Beds</a> are a notable exception &#8212; they can only be made of wood, which also includes the giant mushrooms in the caverns.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>Now would be a good time to start building some <a href="/index.php/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a>. You could queue up all these items directly from your workshops, but why not give your new manager a little practice?
Using the work <span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">o</span></span>rders menu, click the clipboard icon in the top right to queue up a new job, and type "<a href="/index.php/Bed" title="Bed">bed</a>", and then select "Make bed." Click the number sign to set the quantity to around 4 (or more, depending on how many beds you need). Next, queue up at least four <a href="/index.php/Table" title="Table">tables</a>, eight <a href="/index.php/Throne" title="Throne">thrones</a>/chairs, and four doors. Make sure you select a material you have – rock or wood will both work for all of these (except beds), so use whatever you have in your stockpiles. If you like, you can also queue up a few wooden <a href="/index.php/Chest" class="mw-redirect" title="Chest">chests</a> or rock coffers and <a href="/index.php/Cabinet" title="Cabinet">cabinets</a> (which can be used in bedrooms, if you set up individual bedrooms). The tables and chairs will go in your <a href="/index.php/Dining_room" title="Dining room">dining room</a>, speaking of which...
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dining_and_Food_Prep_Area">Dining and Food Prep Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Dining and Food Prep Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Right off the main stairwell (any unused area by the staircase will work), create three rooms. One will be for general food storage, one a <a href="/index.php/Dining_room" title="Dining room">dining hall</a>, and one a <a href="/index.php/Kitchen" title="Kitchen">kitchen</a>. The kitchen will allow you to make <a href="/index.php/Cook#Recipes" title="Cook">prepared food</a>. Make the room for the kitchen 5×5. The storage area and dining hall should be larger. Ideally, leave empty space on at least one side of your dining hall so that it can be expanded later if necessary.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/index.php/File:DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/images/thumb/8/8a/DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png/300px-DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="355" class="thumbimage" srcset="/images/thumb/8/8a/DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png/450px-DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png 1.5x, /images/8/8a/DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png 2x" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/index.php/File:DFwikiDiningFoodPrepExample.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dining level with dining hall (east), kitchen (north), storage area (west), fishery, butcher's workshop, and tanner's workshop (south).</div></div></div>
<p>Use <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bo.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bo.png" src="/images/a/aa/Ui_bo.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">o</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bof.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bof.png" src="/images/0/0a/Ui_bof.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">f</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bofk.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bofk.png" src="/images/a/a2/Ui_bofk.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">k</span></span></span></span></span> to build the kitchen in the middle of the 5×5 room. Use <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_p.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui p.png" src="/images/4/4a/Ui_p.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">p</span></span></span></span></span> to create food stockpiles in the remaining space around it, as well as the entire food storage room. Go back to your general-purpose stockpile on the top level and change the settings to disable food (click "Food" then click "None" in the center column). This will cause any food in your general purpose stockpile to get moved to your new food-only stockpiles. Hit <span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">y</span></span> and select <i><a href="/index.php/Kitchen" title="Kitchen">Kitchen</a></i> from the top of the screen, then disable all cooking for plants, and enable brewing for them so that they will only be used for brewing. Also disable alcoholic beverages for cooking, otherwise your cooks will waste perfectly good hooch in their cooking. The only time you might want to use alcohol in cooking is when you have lots of booze but are running out of food. If you plan to do any fishing, dig out another area and create a <a href="/index.php/Fishery" title="Fishery">Fishery</a> on this level so the uncleaned fish your fisherdwarf just caught can be cleaned (gutted) for consumption or cooking. If you plan to do any hunting or <a href="/index.php/Status#Animal_Status_Screen" title="Status">slaughter</a> any animals, create a <a href="/index.php/Butcher%27s_shop" title="Butcher&#39;s shop">Butcher's shop</a> on this level so animal corpses can be butchered. The fishery/butcher's shop can be placed behind the kitchen or the general food stockpile, for example. A door is recommended for the butcher's shop in order to contain <a href="/index.php/Miasma" title="Miasma">Miasma</a> should something rot, and to otherwise avoid offending squeamish dwarves. Eventually, go check out the subpage on <a href="/index.php/Quickstart_guide/Stockpiles" title="Quickstart guide/Stockpiles">Stockpiles</a> for more information on fine-tuning these stockpiles for maximum efficiency. For now you can safely procrastinate on this and move on to the next section.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Placing_Furniture">Placing Furniture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Placing Furniture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Once your furnishings are complete, you need to place them in rooms using the build furniture (<span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bf.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bf.png" src="/images/b/b0/Ui_bf.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">f</span></span></span></span></span>) command. Put the new chai<span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">r</span></span>s and <span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">t</span></span>ables in the dining room. If you like, you can add doors for aesthetics (they can be useful in case something starts rotting in your food stockpiles). If you created chests and cabinets, you can add them to each room if you want, but it is not urgent now.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meeting_Hall">Meeting Hall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Meeting Hall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Add a Meeting Area <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_z.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui z.png" src="/images/1/13/Ui_z.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="35" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">z</span></span></span></span></span> (zone) in the dining room. This will cause idle dwarves to hang around in the dining hall. You want idlers in a central location, close to where you will be placing your emergency drawbridge levers. You should probably remove the temporary meeting area (and any other meeting areas that you created earlier).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Checking_Supplies">Checking Supplies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Checking Supplies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #a00; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Hostile Wilds</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>Before turning on either hunting or fishing, examine the <span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">u</span></span>nits screen to see if there are any dangerous critters your hunters/fishers need worry about. With hunting especially, you may need to check this screen frequently.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>Use the <a href="/index.php/Stocks" title="Stocks">stoc<span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">k</span></span>s</a> screen to check your stock levels. How much food and booze do you have left? You only have unprepared food at this point, and the booze you brought with you, but soon you will be making more. If you are running low on food, you can designate gathering some <a href="/index.php/Shrub" title="Shrub">outdoor plants</a>, <a href="/index.php/Status#Animal_Status_Screen" title="Status">slaughter</a> some animals, turn on <a href="/index.php/Fishing" class="mw-redirect" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, or turn on <a href="/index.php/Hunting" class="mw-redirect" title="Hunting">hunting</a> to tide you over for a bit. Hunting and slaughtering animals both require a butcher's shop.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brewing_and_Cooking">Brewing and Cooking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Brewing and Cooking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Once your first crop of plump helmets starts to come in, you will want to start <a href="/index.php/Brewing" class="mw-redirect" title="Brewing">brewing</a> as a <a href="/index.php/Repeat" title="Repeat">repeating</a> task. Also, now would be a good time to start <a href="/index.php/Cooking" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooking">cooking</a> actual meals rather than forcing your dwarves to eat raw food. Cooking <a href="/index.php/Cooking#Recipes" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooking">easy meals</a> will train dwarves faster, but they may be happier with <a href="/index.php/Cooking#Recipes" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooking">lavish meals</a>. So, you might want to cook easy ones until your cook or cooks skill up to a certain point then have them start making lavish meals. Prepared food is cooked from two (easy), three (fine), or four (lavish) raw food/alcohol ingredients. Each prepared food item will be called a 'something' (for instance, a specific animal meat) "biscuit", "stew", or "roast" depending on the lavishness of the meal.
</p>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #0a0; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Conserving Resources</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>Some things absolutely require wood (like beds and charcoal), but others can be made out of more common materials like stone. For this reason it's best, especially in the beginning, to make everything that you can out of stone. For example, you could make wood chests and barrels, but stone coffers and rock pots would let you save wood for things that require it and help you rid yourself of all that stone. And if you decide you want solid gold chests or something later when you have more resources, you can always throw out the rock coffers.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>Speaking of booze, in order to keep the booze flowing, you will need to create some <a href="/index.php/Barrel" title="Barrel">barrels</a>, or some stone <a href="/index.php/Pot" class="mw-redirect" title="Pot">pots</a>. Your dwarves should have emptied a few barrels by now to get you started, but you will definitely need more. A <i>lot</i> more.  If you have an abundance of trees, then you can designate some more for cutting, and have your carpenter make a bunch of wooden barrels, but it may be more prudent to make a <a href="/index.php/Craftsdwarf%27s_workshop" title="Craftsdwarf&#39;s workshop">Craftsdwarf's workshop</a>, make sure someone has the <a href="/index.php/Stonecrafting" class="mw-redirect" title="Stonecrafting">Stonecrafting</a> labor enabled, and build a bunch of rock pots. (Rock pots are essentially barrels made of rock.) And don't worry that you've made too many; you almost can't get enough of them. Keep checking your food and drink stock levels on the status bar at the top of the screen periodically. While cooked food (properly stockpiled) and alcohol don't spoil, there is really no need to stock 2,000 units of dwarven wine at this point. Ten times the number of drinks and meals as you have dwarves is more than enough. If you start running out of food or drinks, designate some wild plants for harvesting, <a href="/index.php/Status#Animal_Status_Screen" title="Status">slaughter</a> some of your animals, start hunting or fishing, or start more farms. (Actually, now would be a fine time to make another 3×3 farm. Set it to produce <a href="/index.php/Sweet_pod" title="Sweet pod">sweet pods</a> in the spring and summer, <a href="/index.php/Cave_wheat" title="Cave wheat">cave wheat</a> or <a href="/index.php/Pig_tail" title="Pig tail">pig tails</a> (your choice) in the fall (autumn), and <a href="/index.php/Plump_helmet" title="Plump helmet">plump helmets</a> in the winter. Having multiple types of plants will give your dwarves more variety in their food and drink, keeping them from <a href="/index.php/Thought" title="Thought">grumbling</a>.)
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storage_Space">Storage Space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Storage Space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #0a0; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Advanced Stockpiling</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>Check out the <a href="/index.php/Quickstart_guide/Stockpiles" title="Quickstart guide/Stockpiles">Stockpiles</a> sub-page for more information on fine-tuning your stockpiles, especially in the food production area. This is somewhat complicated and it can safely be skipped if you don't feel like tinkering with stockpiles right now.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>You should probably start making some wooden <b><a href="/index.php/Bin" title="Bin">bins</a></b> to help you store more stuff in less space. You might not need them yet, but you certainly will later. Bins are somewhat like barrels/pots, but they can store things other than just food and drink. Bins will also reduce the amount of labor needed to <a href="/index.php/Haul" class="mw-redirect" title="Haul">haul</a> things to your trade depot or other stockpiles. So designate some more trees to be chopped down and queue up some bins. As with barrels and pots, you almost can't have enough bins.
</p>
<h1><span class="mw-headline" id="Beyond_a_Minimal_Fortress">Beyond a Minimal Fortress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Beyond a Minimal Fortress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1>
<p>By now you should have your main entrance created, along with a farm, general-purpose stockpile, refuse pile (for trash), and <a href="/index.php/Trade_depot" title="Trade depot">trade depot</a>. Somewhere you should have a stoneworker's shop, a mechanic's shop, a carpenter's shop, and a jeweler's shop, surrounded by appropriate storage piles with garbage zone (for excess stone). You should also have a furnished dining area with kitchen, still, and food storage, and a residential area with furnished bedrooms and an office. You should have selected your administrators, and might even have an optional fishery, butcher's shop, craftsdwarf's workshop, or other stuff. At this point, you have all the components of a minimal but functional fortress! Your next steps will be to make it safer and better-protected, to set up your <a href="/index.php/Metal_industry" title="Metal industry">metal industry</a>, and later to prepare your <a href="/index.php/Military" title="Military">militia</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Traps">Traps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Traps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Start producing <b><a href="/index.php/Mechanism" title="Mechanism">mechanisms</a></b> at your <a href="/index.php/Mechanic%27s_workshop" title="Mechanic&#39;s workshop">mechanic's workshop</a>. Queue up ten. After they are built, use them to create <a href="/index.php/Trap#Stone-fall_Trap" title="Trap">stone fall traps</a> using <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bt.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bt.png" src="/images/b/b8/Ui_bt.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">t</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_btt.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui btt.png" src="/images/4/43/Ui_btt.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">t</span></span></span></span></span>. Be sure not to block access to your depot! Queue up some <a href="/index.php/Cage" title="Cage">cages</a>, and more mechanisms, and use these to create some <a href="/index.php/Trap#Cage_Trap" title="Trap">cage traps</a> right after your stone traps. Cage traps are incredibly effective at stopping ambushers, but traps in general will not protect you from <a href="/index.php/Thief" title="Thief">thieves and kidnappers</a> who will almost always bypass them. (To deal with these ambushers, see the next section on <a href="#Guard_Animals">guard animals</a>). Continue to fill up your entry hall with alternating rows of stone and cage traps as the parts become available. Ideally you want to have enough cage traps to take out most of the <a href="/index.php/Goblin" title="Goblin">goblins</a> so your military will only have to mop up.
</p><p>Note that traps will block wagons from reaching your trade depot (although pack animals will still arrive safely). A few ways to avoid this are shown below:
</p>

</tbody></table></div>
</div>
</td>
<td>A more complex design, but also extremely effective (best used underground). The majority of invaders will choose to take the shortest path, directly through the traps. This can also be extended to make a wider group of traps of a longer safe route.
<p>This is relatively easy to implement if you already have a 3-tile wide hallway – just dig a small loop off it and place traps in the old location.
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Note that this is only necessary when caravans can't get to your trade depot, because the hallway is filled with traps - if your trade depot is not behind a trap-lined hallway, you can safely make a hallway full of traps - citizens won't trigger traps.
</p><p>If you place a trap somewhere you didn't mean to, remove it by clicking on it and selecting "Remove this building".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Guard_Animals">Guard Animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Guard Animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Create one 1×1 <a href="/index.php/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a> near the beginning of your entryway, in the middle tile, using <span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_z.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui z.png" src="/images/1/13/Ui_z.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="35" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">z</span></span></span></span></span>. Assign a <a href="/index.php/Dog" title="Dog">dog</a> or other non-grazing animal to it. This animal will spot thieves and raiders before they gain entrance to your fortress. Try to pick a disposable animal, as it <i>will</i> be slaughtered by the first ambush raiders. Ideally, don't assign female animals; you want them safe for <a href="/index.php/Meat_industry#Breeding" title="Meat industry">breeding</a> (you should make sure to keep at least one male around for breeding as well).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Drawbridge">Drawbridge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Drawbridge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In case of an <a href="/index.php/Ambush" title="Ambush">ambush</a> or <a href="/index.php/Siege" title="Siege">siege</a>, you will want to close up your fort, keeping the goblins out until your <a href="/index.php/Squad" title="Squad">squads</a> have formed up and are in position. Therefore, you can build a <a href="/index.php/Bridge" title="Bridge">drawbridge</a> (<span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bn.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bn.png" src="/images/c/c7/Ui_bn.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span></span>) to seal off your entryway. Make sure to set the draw direction, which then forms a barrier to block enemy ranged units. If you don't get the orientation of the bridge correct, it will just retract (disappear) instead of raising up, allowing enemy ranged units to fire across. 
</p><p>Put the drawbridge between the trade depot and the hall-o-traps so you can lock things out of the fort. Build a lever (<span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bm.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bm.png" src="/images/1/1d/Ui_bm.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">m</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bml.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bml.png" src="/images/4/47/Ui_bml.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">l</span></span></span></span></span>) near your meeting area and <a href="/index.php/Lever#Linking" title="Lever">link</a> it to the drawbridge by clicking on the lever and selecting "Link lever". (This linking will require 3 <a href="/index.php/Mechanisms" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanisms">mechanisms</a> in total.)
</p><p>If you used the second design above for your <a href="#Traps">trap hallway</a> then you may want to try adding a second drawbridge in the cutouts for wagon access that can close it off and force invaders through the traps.  Be sure to keep the bridge's orientation in mind.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Metal_Industry">Metal Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Metal Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/index.php/File:DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/images/thumb/4/49/DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png/300px-DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="/images/thumb/4/49/DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png/450px-DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png 1.5x, /images/thumb/4/49/DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png/600px-DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png 2x" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/index.php/File:DFwikiForgesandSmeltersExample.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Level -2: Forge and smelters with bars stockpile in the middle.</div></div></div>
<p>Now, below your first workshop level, dig out four more 5×5 rooms around the stairwell. Three of these will be <a href="/index.php/Smelter" title="Smelter">smelters</a> (<span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">i</span></span></span></span></span>). Designate stockpiles for bars around the smelters and forge. The bar stockpiles will hold <a href="/index.php/Fuel" title="Fuel">coke and charcoal</a> and metal <a href="/index.php/Bar" title="Bar">bars</a>. You will probably need larger bar stockpiles, but you can dig out more space and expand them later. Also dig out some space and create a stockpile for <a href="/index.php/Ore" title="Ore">ore</a> somewhere nearby. To make an ore stockpile, designate a stone stockpile, then change the settings on it to forbid all types of stone other than ore. Finally, go to your general-purpose stockpile on the top level and disable Bars. Stone should already be disabled on this stockpile, and if so, then ore is already disabled for it.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wood_Burning">Wood Burning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Wood Burning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Somewhere near your carpenter's shop, near your wood stockpile, dig out an area and build a <a href="/index.php/Wood_furnace" title="Wood furnace">wood furnace</a> (<span><span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_b.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui b.png" src="/images/b/b1/Ui_b.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">b</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bo.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bo.png" src="/images/a/aa/Ui_bo.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">o</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bou.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bou.png" src="/images/9/90/Ui_bou.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">u</span></span></span></span>-<span style="display: inline-flex;"><a href="/index.php/File:Ui_bouf.png" class="image"><img alt="Ui bouf.png" src="/images/0/06/Ui_bouf.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="32" /></a><span style="align-self: flex-end; margin-left: -3px; margin-bottom: 0px;"><span style="white-space: nowrap;"><span class="keyboard-key nowrap" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; border-radius: 0.2em; -webkit-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-border-radius: 0.2em; -o-border-radius: 0.2em; -ms-border-radius: 0.2em; -moz-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; -webkit-box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; box-shadow: 0.1em 0.2em 0.2em #ddd; background-color: #f9f9f9; background-image: -moz-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -o-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: -webkit-linear-gradient(top, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); background-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #eee, #f9f9f9, #eee); padding: 0.1em 0.3em; font-family: inherit; font-size: 0.9em;" title="">f</span></span></span></span></span>).  This is where you will create charcoal (see below) and ash (for making soap). Dwarf Fortress has two forms of carbon which are useful as <a href="/index.php/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a> in the metal industry: <i>charcoal</i> (which is charred wood), and <i>coke</i> (refined coal).  They are completely interchangeable.  If your map has a lot of <b>lignite</b> or <b>bituminous coal</b>, you can process that into coke, using charcoal to jump-start the process. If you don't find coal on your map, you'll need to either dig down to <a href="/index.php/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a> or make charcoal out of wood to run your forges and smelters, but don't worry about this yet. You need to do some digging around.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #0a0; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>"I have struck what?"</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>New players who don't have a degree in geology usually find themselves confused as to what all these mineral names mean. In DF you'll never strike "iron ore" but you will strike <a href="/index.php/Magnetite" title="Magnetite">magnetite</a> or <a href="/index.php/Limonite" title="Limonite">limonite</a> which are <a href="/index.php/Ore" title="Ore">ores</a> of <a href="/index.php/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>. If you don't know that these things are ores of iron then it obviously won't occur to you to try to smelt iron. See <i><b><a href="/index.php/The_Non-Dwarf%27s_Guide_to_Rock" title="The Non-Dwarf&#39;s Guide to Rock">The Non-Dwarf's Guide to Rock</a></b></i> to help you figure out exactly what you've found.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>At this point you want to start looking for metal ore. You may have already found some while digging out rooms, in which case you can just mine into the walls of the rooms to get more ore. If you haven't found ore yet or you want to see what else you can find, you will need to dig <a href="/index.php/Exploratory_mining" title="Exploratory mining">exploratory tunnels</a> looking for ores, minerals, and <a href="/index.php/Gem" title="Gem">gems</a>. For now just start digging tunnels out from your stairwell or rooms in all directions and see what you run into. Note that digging into <b>damp stone</b> or <b>warm stone</b> is not recommended as those areas may be holding back water or lava which can flood your fort.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel">Fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Whether you find <a href="/index.php/Coal" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal">coal</a> or not, you will need to burn wood into at least one unit of <a href="/index.php/Charcoal" class="mw-redirect" title="Charcoal">charcoal</a>. If you find some coal (<a href="/index.php/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> or <a href="/index.php/Bituminous_coal" title="Bituminous coal">bituminous coal</a>), start your <a href="/index.php/Smelter" title="Smelter">smelters</a> out processing it into <a href="/index.php/Coke" class="mw-redirect" title="Coke">coke</a> using your charcoal to get things started. From then out you can burn coke to make more coal into more coke and so on. Put these coke-making jobs on repeat. Only use one smelter to begin with, but you should be getting a group of <a href="/index.php/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrants</a> fairly soon, if you haven't already, and you can put them to work in the other smelters. Don't give up on finding coal right away. Dig around for a while and if you're starting to get impatient then burn some more wood into charcoal, smelt some ore, and make some <a href="/index.php/Weapon" title="Weapon">weapons</a>. If you rely on charcoal for fuel then you'll be needing a <i>lot</i> of wood, so in that case dig out another room near the furnace and create a wood stockpile. You might also want to just remove a smelter, replace it with a <a href="/index.php/Wood_furnace" title="Wood furnace">wood furnace</a>, and create the new wood stockpile down in the smelting area. Finally, go designate more trees for chopping.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forging">Forging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Forging">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #0a0; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Alternative Energy</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>If you don't find coal then you will have to continue to burn wood into charcoal, or dig down to the bottom of the map and find the magma sea so you can power <a href="/index.php/Magma_smelter" title="Magma smelter">magma smelters</a> and <a href="/index.php/Magma_forge" title="Magma forge">magma forges</a>. Getting to magma can be difficult for various reasons that you will discover, so make sure you are ready for some trouble before you go that direction. Burning charcoal should work out okay in the short term.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>Once you have smelted some ore to get metal bars, and have additional bars of either coal or charcoal, you can start forging metal items. Here are some suggestions on what to make first:
</p>
<ol><li><b><a href="/index.php/Pick" title="Pick">Picks</a></b> - You may have only started out with one pick which limits the number of miners you have to one. By this point you are probably wishing you had more miners. Make a few picks and give some dwarves the mining labor once you get some immigrants. It doesn't matter what metal you use to make picks, at least when it comes to mining, so even copper is perfectly good.</li>
<li><b><a href="/index.php/Weapon" title="Weapon">Weapons</a></b> - Picks actually make pretty good weapons, but there can be some issues equipping them because they're tied to the mining labor. You may want to make a few axes. They make good weapons, at least against most lightly armored opponents you're likely to encounter first, and can be used to chop trees. Start with 5 or so.</li>
<li><b><a href="/index.php/Armor" title="Armor">Armor</a></b> - You're going to want some armor. Start with mail shirts, helms, leggings, then gauntlets and boots. Start with 3 or so of each in the order listed, then make more later when your military grows.  Also make some shields out of wood, unless you're swimming in metal (since the shield's material doesn't matter for defensive purposes).  Once you have the essentials covered, you can include breastplates (but they take 3 bars of metal to make, and they don't cover as much of the torso and arms as a mail shirt).</li></ol>
<p>An important thing to note is that mail shirts protect the upper leg as well as the torso and arms, and high boots protect the lower leg. As dwarves have no knees (at least in military terms), high boots and mail shirts are sufficient to protect your dwarves' legs.
<a href="/index.php/Steel" title="Steel">Steel</a> is the best normal metal to make armor and most weapons out of, but you will likely find that you want some arms before you can make steel. <a href="/index.php/Iron" title="Iron">Iron</a> is good, as is <a href="/index.php/Bronze" title="Bronze">bronze</a>. <a href="/index.php/Copper" title="Copper">Copper</a> is not ideal, but it still works and is better than no metal weapons/armor at all.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gemcutting_and_Trinkets">Gemcutting and Trinkets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Gemcutting and Trinkets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/index.php/File:DFwikiCraftsExample.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="/images/thumb/8/82/DFwikiCraftsExample.png/300px-DFwikiCraftsExample.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="/images/8/82/DFwikiCraftsExample.png 1.5x" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/index.php/File:DFwikiCraftsExample.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A craftsdwarf workshop. They produce crafts and trinkets which can be traded in a Depot.</div></div></div>
<p>You should have uncovered some <a href="/index.php/Gem" title="Gem">gems</a> by now, so put your <a href="/index.php/Jeweler" title="Jeweler">jeweler</a> to work <a href="/index.php/Gem_cutter" title="Gem cutter">cutting</a> them. These will be used for <a href="/index.php/Trading" title="Trading">trade</a>.  Only buy things that you need in the first year. <a href="/index.php/Finished_goods" title="Finished goods">Stone crafts</a> produced by a craftsdwarf can make good trading goods as well. To get enough goods, you will need to dedicate a craftsdwarf's workshop and craftsdwarf to this task full-time, but you're very unlikely to ever run out of stone.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sticking_to_the_Plan">Sticking to the Plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Sticking to the Plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #a00; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Getting Distracted</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>Say one of your new immigrants turns out to be a legendary weaver. Should you plant some pig tails and create a loom for him? <b>No!</b> Put his legendary butt to work smelting metal or something that's part of your current industry even though he has no skill at it. Do not split your efforts yet. You can make use of his unique talents later when you can afford to diversify your industry.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>Metalsmithing will be your primary economic activity, with cutting gems (and possibly making stone crafts) being used to give you some short-term <a href="/index.php/Wealth" title="Wealth">wealth</a> until the <a href="/index.php/Metal_industry" title="Metal industry">metal industry</a> gets going. This means you will need miners, haulers, smiths and furnace operators. Unless a dwarf is doing something else vital to the proper functioning of your fort, such as training in the militia, making traps, cooking food, and so forth, they should be doing one of those four things.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wealth_and_Invasion">Wealth and Invasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Wealth and Invasion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div style="float: right; clear:right; border: 2px solid black; background: white; margin: 1em; margin-right:0em; width: 35%;">
<div style="background: #a00; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; border-bottom: 1px solid black; text-align: center; font-size:120%; color:#ffffff"><b>Crafting Invitations for Trouble</b></div>
<div style="padding: 0 0.5em;">
<p>Creating too much wealth initially is a sure fire method of pulling down a goblin ambush that you are ill-equipped to deal with. Titans will also start attacking you should your wealth go over a certain amount. For this reason, spend no time smelting gold, smoothing, or engraving anything yet. Most of the wealth you create in the beginning should be the <a href="/index.php/Weapon" title="Weapon">sharp pointy kind</a>.
</p>
</div>
</div>
<p>You may have struck <a href="/index.php/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> or some other valuable metal, and you may be tempted to put your furnaces and smiths to work creating valuable metal crafts. Don't do it! Until you have your militia formed and fully equipped with armor and weaponry, your smelters and forge should be doing nothing else but smelting cheaper materials like coal, iron, making pig iron and steel if possible, and making weapons and armor. Making <a href="/index.php/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> will actually increase your wealth quite a bit, but at least you can stab and beat things to death with steel; you can't make weapons from gold.
</p>
<h1><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1>
<p>Your <b>military</b> is an important part of fortress defense. Unless you have totally cut yourself off from the outside world, then you will want at least some sort of military. Once you reach this point, you should hopefully have enough dwarves to start a small military training program. You will need at least 5 dwarves who aren't otherwise doing anything important. If you don't have any spare dwarves yet, or just don't want to mess with it yet, just skip to the next section and come back to this later. Don't wait too long to set up your military though; you especially will want soldiers before you reach a population of 80 dwarves. (You will find out why.) When you're ready to start up your military, see the <a href="/index.php/Military_quickstart" title="Military quickstart">Military quickstart</a> guide.
</p>
<h1><span id="What_Next?"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="What_Next.3F">What Next?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: What Next?">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1>
<p>Congratulations! If you've made it this far then you have a self-sustaining fort going and can now start to branch out into whatever you are interested in exploring. Expect some goblin invasions, forgotten beasts, titans, dragons, giants, and other creatures to interrupt your activities at various points. This is part of the <a href="/index.php/Fun" class="mw-redirect" title="Fun">fun</a>.
</p><p>Here are some things that people almost always do eventually, though not necessarily in any particular order (these are somewhat essential):
</p>
<ul><li>Build <a href="/index.php/Coffin" title="Coffin">coffins</a> and a graveyard or <a href="/index.php/Tomb" title="Tomb">tombs</a> for dead dwarves and pets</li>
<li>Set up a <a href="/index.php/Healthcare" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare">hospital</a></li>
<li>Build a <a href="/index.php/Well" title="Well">well</a></li>
<li>Start producing <a href="/index.php/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">clothing</a> to replace <a href="/index.php/Wear" title="Wear">worn-out attire</a></li>
<li>Build a <a href="/index.php/Jail" class="mw-redirect" title="Jail">jail</a> for unruly dwarves</li>
<li>Set up <a href="/index.php/Scheduling#Alert_Levels" title="Scheduling">civilian alerts</a> to get civilians to a safe area during ambushes and sieges</li></ul>
<p>Here are some things that players often do as their population grows:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/index.php/Smoothing" title="Smoothing">Smooth</a> and <a href="/index.php/Engraving" title="Engraving">engrave</a> walls and floors</li>
<li>Produce <a href="/index.php/Meat_industry" title="Meat industry">Meat</a>, <a href="/index.php/Egg_production" title="Egg production">eggs</a>, milk and <a href="/index.php/Beekeeping_industry" title="Beekeeping industry">honey</a></li>
<li>Continue to expand the <a href="/index.php/Military" title="Military">military</a></li>
<li>Explore new <a href="/index.php/Industry" title="Industry">industries</a></li>
<li>Dig down to the <a href="/index.php/Caverns" class="mw-redirect" title="Caverns">caverns</a> and create a defended lower entrance with traps to defend the fort against the <a href="/index.php/Creatures" title="Creatures">denizens</a> below</li>
<li>Enable <a href="/index.php/Animal_training" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal training">Animal training</a> for a dwarf and train some war animals</li>
<li>Build a <a href="/index.php/Mass_pitting" title="Mass pitting">Mass pitting</a> system to dispose of caged enemies</li>
<li>Build above-ground <a href="/index.php/Construction" title="Construction">constructions</a> such as an archery tower or garden</li>
<li>Create a <a href="/index.php/Statue" title="Statue">statue garden</a> or <a href="/index.php/Zoo" title="Zoo">zoo</a></li>
<li>Farm in an <a href="/index.php/Farming#Above-ground_farming" title="Farming">above-ground farm plot</a></li>
<li>Dig down to <a href="/index.php/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a> and set up <a href="/index.php/Magma_forge" title="Magma forge">magma forges</a> and <a href="/index.php/Magma_smelter" title="Magma smelter">magma smelters</a> to avoid the need for fuel</li>
<li>Build <a href="/index.php/Machine_component" title="Machine component">machine components</a> to pump magma and water</li>
<li>Create more <a href="/index.php/Trap_design" title="Trap design">elaborate traps</a> such as magma and drowning chambers</li>
<li>Try some <a href="/index.php/Stupid_dwarf_trick" title="Stupid dwarf trick">stupid dwarf tricks</a></li></ul>
<p>You may also want to just read over the <a href="/index.php/Dwarf_fortress_mode" title="Dwarf fortress mode">Fortress Mode Reference Guide</a> and the many other very useful documents on the wiki to give you other ideas of what to do.
</p><p>Keep in mind that how you play is not set in stone. Some people never defend, some start a <a href="/index.php/Megaprojects" class="mw-redirect" title="Megaprojects">megaproject</a> right after settling, some never dig and just build an above ground castle or town using logs. Some never smelt ore, some start smelting as soon as they arrive. Some make their home in the dangerous natural caverns. Some deal with invaders by flooding the map or isolating themselves completely. And that's not even considering the <a href="/index.php/List_of_mods" title="List of mods">mods</a> and some of the crazier <a href="/index.php/Challenges" class="mw-redirect" title="Challenges">challenges</a> that people have come up with. There's really no one "right" way to play DF.
</p>
<h1><span class="mw-headline" id="Feedback">Feedback</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/index.php?title=Quickstart_guide&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Feedback">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h1>
<p>If you have any feedback on this guide, you can leave a message on the <a href="/index.php/Talk:Quickstart_guide" title="Talk:Quickstart guide">talk page</a> for this article.
</p>
<div style="width:60%; margin:auto;">

	<h3 id="p-variants-label">
		<span>Variants</span>
	</h3>
